# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive answer document at `/workspace/answer.json` that maps all Java source files implementing SASL broker-side authentication in Apache Kafka.

## Summary

The document includes **35 source files** across these key categories:

### Core Components:
- **SaslServerAuthenticator** - Main broker-side SASL authenticator managing the complete authentication lifecycle
- **SaslChannelBuilder** - Mechanism selection and server configuration
- **Authentication contexts** - SaslAuthenticationContext and ReauthenticationContext for managing credential lifecycle

### SASL Mechanisms (PLAIN, SCRAM, GSSAPI, OAuthBearer):
- **PLAIN**: PlainSaslServer, PlainServerCallbackHandler, PlainSaslServerProvider
- **SCRAM**: ScramSaslServer, ScramServerCallbackHandler, ScramMechanism, ScramFormatter
- **GSSAPI**: KerberosClientCallbackHandler, KerberosLogin, KerberosShortNamer, KerberosName
- **OAuthBearer**: OAuthBearerSaslServer, OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider, BrokerJwtValidator

### Principal & Authorization:
- **DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder** - Constructs authenticated principals
- **KafkaPrincipalBuilder** - Pluggable principal builder interface

### Supporting Infrastructure:
- Configuration classes, JAAS context management, callback handlers, and authentication interfaces

The document provides a complete mapping showing how Kafka brokers implement pluggable SASL authentication with support for multiple mechanisms, including the mechanism selection flow, server initialization, and re-authentication lifecycle.

implements SASL broker-side authentication through a comprehensive architecture spanning mechanism selection, server authenticator lifecycle, and multiple authentication protocols.\\n\\n## Core SASL Server Authenticator\\n\\nThe **SaslServerAuthenticator** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java) is the primary broker-side SASL authenticator implementing the Authenticator interface. It manages the complete authentication lifecycle:\\n- Handles SASL_HANDSHAKE requests to negotiate the authentication mechanism\\n- Processes SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests for the actual authentication protocol\\n- Creates and manages javax.security.sasl.SaslServer instances\\n- Manages authentication state transitions through defined internal states (INITIAL_REQUEST, SEND_HANDSHAKE, etc.)\\n- Implements re-authentication via the reauthenticate method that consumes ReauthenticationContext\\n\\n## Mechanism Selection and Channel Builder\\n\\nThe **SaslChannelBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java) is responsible for mechanism selection and server setup:\\n- Reads configured enabled mechanisms (sasl.enabled.mechanisms config)\\n- Creates server callback handlers for each enabled mechanism via createServerCallbackHandlers\\n- Instantiates the appropriate mechanism implementation based on JAAS configuration\\n- Manages JAAS context loading for both SERVER and CLIENT contexts\\n- Creates instances of SaslServerAuthenticator via buildServerAuthenticator\\n\\nThe **ChannelBuilders** factory (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java) coordinates creation based on security protocol and creates the principal builder instance.\\n\\n## SASL Mechanism Implementations\\n\\n### PLAIN Mechanism\\n- **PlainSaslServer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java): Implements SaslServer for PLAIN mechanism (RFC 4616)\\n- **PlainServerCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java): Implements AuthenticateCallbackHandler, handles NameCallback and PlainAuthenticateCallback\\n- **PlainSaslServerProvider** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServerProvider.java): Java Security Provider registering PlainSaslServerFactory\\n- **PlainLoginModule** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/PlainLoginModule.java): JAAS LoginModule for PLAIN configuration\\n\\n### SCRAM Mechanisms (SCRAM-SHA-256, SCRAM-SHA-512)\\n- **ScramSaslServer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java): Implements SaslServer for SCRAM mechanisms with ScramSaslServerFactory inner class\\n- **ScramServerCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java): Implements AuthenticateCallbackHandler with credential cache integration\\n- **ScramSaslServerProvider** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServerProvider.java): Java Security Provider registering factories for both SCRAM mechanisms\\n- **ScramMechanism** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMechanism.java): Enum defining SCRAM_SHA_256 and SCRAM_SHA_512 with type identifiers and hash algorithms\\n- **ScramFormatter** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramFormatter.java): PBKDF2 credential formatting\\n- **ScramLoginModule** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/ScramLoginModule.java): JAAS LoginModule for SCRAM configuration\\n\\n### GSSAPI (Kerberos) Mechanism\\n- **KerberosClientCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosClientCallbackHandler.java): Implements AuthenticateCallbackHandler for GSSAPI\\n- **KerberosLogin** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosLogin.java): JAAS Login for Kerberos including keytab/ticket support\\n- **KerberosShortNamer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosShortNamer.java): Maps Kerberos principals to short names using configurable rules\\n- **KerberosName** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosName.java): Parses and represents Kerberos principal components\\n- **KerberosError** and **KerberosRule** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/): Supporting classes for Kerberos authentication\\n\\n### OAuthBearer Mechanism\\n- **OAuthBearerSaslServer** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java): Implements SaslServer for OAUTHBEARER with OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory\\n- **OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider.java): Java Security Provider for OAuthBearer\\n- **OAuthBearerLoginModule** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/OAuthBearerLoginModule.java): JAAS LoginModule\\n- **OAuthBearerLoginCallbackHandler** and **BrokerJwtValidator**: Handle token validation and JWT processing\\n\\n## Authentication Context Lifecycle\\n\\n**SaslAuthenticationContext** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java):\\n- Encapsulates the authenticated SaslServer, SecurityProtocol, client address, and optional SSL session\\n- Passed to KafkaPrincipalBuilder to construct the authenticated principal\\n\\n**ReauthenticationContext** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ReauthenticationContext.java):\\n- Manages re-authentication lifecycle with reference to previous Authenticator\\n- Carries SASL handshake NetworkReceive from re-authentication initiation\\n- Provides timestamp for session expiration tracking\\n\\n**Authenticator Interface** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Authenticator.java):\\n- Base interface with authenticate() and reauthenticate(ReauthenticationContext) methods\\n- Supports authentication lifecycle and periodic re-authentication\\n\\n## Principal Building\\n\\n**DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java):\\n- Implements KafkaPrincipalBuilder interface\\n- Creates KafkaPrincipal from SaslAuthenticationContext\\n- Applies KerberosShortNamer for GSSAPI principals\\n- Extracts authorization ID from SaslServer.getAuthorizationID()\\n- Supports token authentication for SCRAM mechanisms\\n\\n**KafkaPrincipalBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/KafkaPrincipalBuilder.java):\\n- Interface for custom principal builders\\n- Configured via principal.builder.class broker config\\n\\n## Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n**AuthenticateCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/AuthenticateCallbackHandler.java): Interface implemented by all mechanism callback handlers\\n\\n**SaslServerCallbackHandler** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java): Default callback handler for mechanisms without specific handlers\\n\\n**BrokerSecurityConfigs** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/internals/BrokerSecurityConfigs.java): Configuration constants including SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG, SASL_MECHANISM_INTER_BROKER_PROTOCOL_CONFIG, and PRINCIPAL_BUILDER_CLASS_CONFIG\\n\\n**JaasContext** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java): Manages JAAS configuration context with support for static and dynamic configurations\\n\\nThe architecture enables a pluggable mechanism system where each SASL mechanism is registered as a Java Security Provider (PlainSaslServerProvider, ScramSaslServerProvider, OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider), allowing Sasl.createSaslServer() to instantiate the appropriate mechanism implementation based on negotiated mechanism name. The SaslServerAuthenticator orchestrates the protocol exchange, while callback handlers and login modules handle mechanism-specific credential validation.\"\n}\n",

authenticator implementing the Authenticator interface. It manages the complete authentication lifecycle:\\n- Handles SASL_HANDSHAKE requests to negotiate the authentication mechanism\\n- Processes SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests for the actual authentication protocol\\n- Creates and manages javax.security.sasl.SaslServer instances\\n- Manages authentication state transitions through defined internal states (INITIAL_REQUEST, SEND_HANDSHAKE, etc.)\\n- Implements re-authentication via the reauthenticate method that consumes ReauthenticationContext\\n\\n## Mechanism Selection and Channel Builder\\n\\nThe **SaslChannelBuilder** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java) is responsible for mechanism selection and server setup:\\n- Reads configured enabled mechanisms (sasl.enabled.mechanisms config)\\n- Creates server callback handlers for each enabled mechanism via createServerCallbackHandlers\\n- Instantiates the appropriate mechanism implementation based on JAAS configuration\\n- Manages JAAS context loading for both SERVER and CLIENT contexts\\n- Creates instances of SaslServerAuthenticator via buildServerAuthenticator\\n\\nThe **ChannelBuilders** factory (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java) coordinates creation based on security protocol and creates the principal builder instance.\\n\\n## SASL Mechanism
